"Well, we aren't going to get either of those things standing here like we're lost." Mara broke into Xavier's wondering concentration. "Let's head up the street." She cocked a clawed thumb. "I saw a Medicant.  They probably have postcards there and local brochures.  Maybe we can get a general route to take to Pathosia.  That place always has a sister store in town, and they show you it on a map with other landmarks.  It'll be there as soon as we walk in."
"Maybe they have some Nasil." Gabriel said. "I didn't think to bring any from home.  I mean, I didn't know we'd be gone so long."
"Are your allergies still bothering you?  It's fall now."
"Indoor ones, too.  Not as bad, but every now and again I go into a fit of sneezing."
"I know you do." And at this point, Xavier felt very much outside of this conversation and considered if it would be more inappropriate to walk away or to stick around.
"Fine." Xavier says and pivots the balls of his feet and starts walking.  He's not comfortable standing around.  Mara strides past him, and Gabe follows suit.
Five
The drugstore is white and bright and chalked full of cream colored bottles on ramshackle shelves.  There are butterfly catching nets in a bin with plastic bats next to the shampoo aisle.  A separate aisle, the only one predominately not screaming white, is filled with cheap cards and little envelopes.  There is a steel wired bin full of harvest decorations, which are mostly orange.  Gabriel searches the allergy/indigestion aisle for his medication, while Mara examines the map hanging over the wall behind the front counter register.  An old elven man with a freckled, or maybe liver spotted face is standing ready by the register with his hands behind his back.  He is regarding Xavier, who is standing apart from Mara with his arms crossed and his chin tilted toward the shelves of candy bars and mini bags of chips sitting on his side of the counter.
"There's an Inn and Out a few blocks away.  Other than that, there's an Aristocrus on the other side of town, but that's pricey." Mara shifts her weight.  She is in a drugstore with a high powered rifle strapped to her back.
"You folks visiting?" The old elf asks.
"Yeah." Xavier says without looking up.  He is studying the beef jerky prices and trying to remember what he paid last time.  He just ate, but he thinks he could go for some jerky in a little while.
"For the Steel Forest concert?"
Mara, who actually listened to that washed up old rock band, replied. "Yup.  We're all big fans, really looking forward to the new album."
Xavier didn't know how she could listen to that with how good her ears must be.  The old man goes on, "You three be careful tonight.  The Panthedome will be flooding over."
Has Siegfried been pumping these people with Greek?
Mara answers, "Front row tickets."
"Well, I hope you guys have a good time.  Steel Forest was my favorite band for a long time." Then the old man segues. "So did you need anything or-"
"Just checking the map, and Al's getting his allergy medicine so he doesn't blow snot all over the drums."

Chapter Twelve

One
They checked into a room at the Inn and Out.  Room number six by the pool filled with leaves that needed drained soon.  The clerk asked Xavier if two beds would be fine, and Gabe said that it was.  The place sat between a vacant lot with the sign "Wardrobe Emporium Coming Soon!" in it, and a grocery store that had petrol pumps under lock and key by the back door.  The clerk asked Xavier for a photo ID, and he gave it.  It was a real ID, but everything on it was fake.  They paid in cash.
Xavier was given the key, which was a green thing with flakes of white paint peeling off of it.  When he opened the door to the dark room, he heard something scuttle under something else.  He killed it with a thought and its many kin that were living in the wall, no effort there.  He turned on a light, Gabe stood at the door, and Mara walked past the second bed and pulled the seemingly imaginary rifle from her back and rested it against the wall that was now insulated by a dead colony of circular shaped roaches.
"I forgot you still . . ." Gabriel paused and looked about, "had that thing to be honest."
"Never leave home without it." She said, and Xavier thought he detected a bit of huskiness to her voice.  He wanted to move, as standing between the two during this foreplay made him uneasy.  She went on, "But lugging this around all day and night is getting annoying.  Do you think it'll be okay here while we grab supplies?"
There was a moment or two of Xavier being perceptibly lost in thought.  He'd reasoned with himself that his companions were sharing a personal dialogue and let himself wander.  For that brief moment before he answered her, he was wondering if Salina would ever talk to him that way.  Or any woman, really.  Cathrine was on his mind, too, comparing relationships.  Then he heard Mara's question resonate in his ear.  He did what he could to make himself appear to be thinking about it, though he knew right away. "Yeah," He bit down on his lower lip and looked up at the ceiling.  Good show you're putting on.  Feels very genuine. "should be fine."
"What should we do now?" Gabe asked, leaning against the threshold.
"What time is it?" None of them had a watch or a phone handy.  Xavier scanned the room for a clock.
There was an ornate two hand clock composed of what appeared to be shadows at Gabe's feet. "Quarter till one." He said and mumbled something.  The clock faded.
Neat trick.  You'll have to log that one away for later.  Bet you won't even need to recite like he does. "That's convenient." Xavier touched his chin.  There was a thick stubble coming in on his face that he wasn't making grow out the way he was his artificial hair.  He'd forgotten about that piece of nature. "Is there a bathroom back there?" To Mara who was closest to a little corner with a door at the back of the room.  She opened the door and nodded. "A shower?" He asked, and she nodded again. "Then I'm going to get cleaned up.  I know I don't reek, but I've built up a layer of crust.  The two of you just stink." He smiled and realized that they were becoming friends. "If you guys take one after me, we'll probably want to go find clothes next."
Xavier entered the bathroom and closed the door.
Two
The room was small, the toilet had no lid, and the sink was made of plywood with a plastic basin.  The shower had no curtain or door, and its head was pointed at the wall so as to not cover the floor in water.  No complementary bottle of shampoo or a bar of soap, just a crack in the corner where a yellow crust was erupting.  A mirror above the sink wore a gray coat of film like solid condensation.  There were stains on the floor and walls, most looking like barbecue sauce.
He turned on the nozzle and let the cold water bounce against the shower wall.
When Xavier finished, he noticed that there were no towels in the bathroom.  For that matter there wasn't toilet paper either, things to be picked up if they all wanted to take another shower in the morning.  
He's not the kind of clean he would like to be that comes with the soaps and such, but he's taken off his layer of crud.  He evaporates the water from his skin.  Then he slips his old clothes back on.  They should be musty with his odor, but he's been making sure that they wouldn't be.  Now the room is damp, and there is no window to let the steam out.
Mara goes after him, and the two novians sit across from each on respective beds and watch the outdated television.  A midafternoon show about an ex-Leviathan who now does counseling for criminally dramatic individuals is playing.  It is set in a large room with an audience.  The set itself is an absolutely plush looking assortment of chairs and a couch.  The former Leviathan, a rather dweebish looking elf, is sitting in his chair with his cup of coffee beside him on a little oak stand.  Sitting on the couch is a young couple of aemon, a scrawny man and pudgy woman.  The woman is going on and on about her friend Marten and how Iticus (Xavier assumes by her body language that this is the scrawny man next to her) won't stop spending time with him.  She claims that she is convinced Iticus is no longer interested in her or women, and that he is hiding feelings about Marten.  The scrawny man denies this and claims that Marten and he are good friends and that from time to time he is simply tired of Aeria.  He goes on to say that she never wants to do any of the things he wants to do anymore and, get this, he's upset about it.  All the while the quack therapist is nodding and sipping at his cup of sludge, pretending that he had at least some semblance of understanding.  The host then puts down his drink, the audience is on the edge of their seats waiting for him to call the situation, and he announces that someone is in the back and would like to speak with the couple.  Dead silence from the audience, a real whammy must be coming.  Enter left stage, behind the elf comes an aemon man in jean shorts and a pink shirt tied up on his chest like a bra.  He is wearing makeup and swinging his hips femininely as he walks to a chair adjacent of the host's.  The elf tells Marten that he is welcome on the show after the audience stops whistling and screaming as if they've all been given free mansions.  The elf goes for a handshake but receives a hug, and then both sit down.  Iticus is now looking away shamefully and, of course, he'll be next up to bat with a "So what do you and Marten do that Aeria doesn't want to?"
Xavier changes the station by moving the knob on the TV telekinetically.  He's trying to be careful, because after that sideshow he is afraid he might tear the box of wires and gas apart.  There is a soap opera on where people are well lit in what looks like an impossibly dark room, there is a children's show about a talking tiger who guards the Dark Forest with math and vocabulary lessons, a few static channels, and an appraisal show showcasing cheesy jewelry in rotating glass displays.  He looks at Gabe, who is now smirking, and asks, "Anything you want to watch?"
"Are you kidding me?  Channel seven with the snow static is a hit.  I can't get enough of that." He laid down on top of the bedspread. "The rest of those shows were trash though."
Xavier leans back against the headboard of his own bed.  These two that he's been assigned with are turning out to be fine people.  He flips through the stations again and pauses on the drama therapy show, meaning to shut the thing off in the same place he turned it on.  But the stuff shirt elf and his clan of society's paid acting dregs are nowhere to be seen.  Commercials are on and are somehow more entertaining than the show.  The screen goes black after a fair voiced young woman finishes her listing of endless side effects from an antacid, and soulful music begins playing.  A dwarven man and his family are standing outside of their home, a deteriorating trailer, and huddled together like refugees.  He begins talking about how mismanaged the country has been between Trothos and Dahzir.  "It's hard just to keep up with the taxes." He says and goes on that none of it goes back to the people.  A slideshow of busted up roads and raggedy children starts, and Xavier is reminded of charity drives he used to see on earth.  Then they show some of the more opulent cities, governors' city-states and especially the few that were run by the royal family.  There is contrast, it shows, of lavish cities with cars and fine houses and towns that can't afford shoes.  The man says, "We are one country, one world.  But we are divided.  We need leaders that will put us first.  We need order." The screen fades a bit, the slideshow resumes, and the music goes up just a decibel or two and is now in a violin section, which Xavier thinks might be the very instrument of sadness.  Large white letters phase onto the screen, contrasted by the somber background.  It reads, "We need unity and fairness." These fade away and are replaced by "We need The Order." A few more seconds of music, the letters fade away, and Xavier kills the TV's power.
"That is so true." Gabe said still staring at the ceiling. "There are places where no one can afford to feed their families, but they work three jobs all day.  The next town over, and you might manage just fine with one job.  It might even be the same job."
Xavier begins to nod off.  He's tired from the train ride, from his responsibilities, and thoughts.  The bed under him is not comfortable, but compared to the cab seats, it is a luxury mattress.

Three
He is standing at the edge of a cliffside overlooking a vast ocean.  The sky above him is a lifeless teal color under an unending expanse of foreboding clouds.  Waves crash up against the rocks below, furious but powerless against the land.  He looks down and sees a nondescript pair of pants under a black shirt with a mural of a snowy field.  He is not wearing shoes.  Then he notices he is not guised as the novian he calls Xavier and tries to shift, but there is no magic here, so he remains Cecil.
The air is impossibly refreshing on his skin, and he feels charged with a bottomless strength.  An urge to leap from the cliff washes over him, as he knows that if he jumped he would be able to fly.  He would soar over that gray ocean and let the salty winds run through his scalp.  He feels invincible.
There comes a footstep, soft and steady, behind him.  He doesn't look back, and somehow he knows he doesn't need to.  He is overwhelmed with joy that he can be back here on Earth with them.  Cecil can't seem to remember what all he's done since Sul, but the concern is meaningless to him.  A warm pair of hands wrap around his waist, and Salina props her head on his shoulder.  They don't speak but simply enjoy the view.
He looks at her, unable to express how happy he is to see her, but she understands the smile on his face and returns it.  He feels her press into his back, and he loves her warmth.  His hands go down and cover hers, and he tilts his head so that he is just barely resting against hers.
Cecil notices that her head has changed to its wolf shape and that Salina is now covered in fur.  Her tail wraps around him and goes overtop his hands.  She says something with her body language that he can't put into words, but he does know how to react.  He tries to transform the way she did, the way he once had.  But he cannot.  He looks at her sorrowfully, almost apologetically, but she is undeterred.  They embrace, and everything feels perfectly aligned to him.
Four
"Xav, you ready to go?" Gabriel asks, almost at the door.  Mara is next to him, smoothing the matted fur behind her ears.
"Huh." Xavier mumbles.  He can answer now, but he takes a moment to wish the dream hadn't ended.  He knows if it gets continued later, he won't remember. "Yeah, just a little groggy."

Chapter Thirteen

One
He never did enjoy clothes shopping.  Despite what it was for, it was no more enjoyable.  At least it was easy to find clothing for novians, but wasn't sure of what kind.  The other two didn't seem to be going through the same thought process as Xavier.  For him this was not merely finding things to cover up with but to be in cover with.  Did he want to buy jeans and T-shirts and look like a normal citizen, or did he want to dress up another notch, maybe to look like a health inspector or an upbeat entrepreneur.  He supposed he could dial it up a little higher even, throw in some of that mind bending power he seemed to have, and he could be a real go-getter, an executive or an impersonator for one of governor's aids.
Keep it simple.  He told himself and grabbed the working man pants and shirts.
Two
When they got back to the motel, he told them that they should spend the day learning what they could and, in general, relax.  It might be the last day they wouldn't be walking on ice.
They went their way, and he went his.  Truthfully he just wanted some time alone, time in which he could think and no one would try to pry his thoughts off of him with their metaphorical pennies.
He was thinking of her too much and too often.  Xavier was afraid that he might become obsessed and do something regrettable.  He'd begun having dreams about her, so how long would it be before he started acting out on his fondness, before he started writing letters and sending her clips of hair?  He thought never, but four years ago he would have said that he would never be a werewolf or a wizard, or come back to life on a technicality.  If he really felt for her, and he wasn't so sure he trusted his feelings, then perhaps it wasn't so unhealthy.  He didn't believe in falling in love through kindness or friendships or heroic deeds.  You either liked someone and could build onto that, or you didn't.
He needed some time to straighten this all out.
Three
Xavier finds himself in a park with lush grass and symmetrical trees.  After the wasteland, he never thought he'd see the green again.  There is a draken man sitting in the grass under an orange leafed oak; he is surrounded by acorns and playing an acoustic guitar.  The man has no turned up hat or guitar case at his feet.  He is playing just for the fun of it.  There is a fountain with its water source cut off, but there are still pigeons perched at the font waiting for handouts to come from the benches.
The park is not private enough.  It is a fine fall afternoon, and leafers are strolling through, gawking at all the colors and "Can you believe they turned like this?" They do every year.  He wants to be back in the Glade, where he could keep his own counsel.
It is still somewhat early in the afternoon when Xavier reaches the theater.  There is nothing good playing, but he buys a ticket for a low budget film.  The ticket man asks for an ID, but Xavier is tired of showing that false piece of plastic and shoots him a look that almost knocks the aemon off his stool.  The man lets Xavier in, forgetting the ID and what he had for breakfast.
The lobby appears clean, but the lights are dim and he doesn't think this is for cinematic effect.  There is a snack island in the center, complete with a popcorn machine and a pop fountain with an accompanying tub of ice.  There are two workers at this station, a tall elven man and a younger female ogre.  They are not busy in the slightest, and Xavier wonders why they need two people working now.  His screen is at the end of the lobby on the right side, and in between are old arcade machines, two of which are out of order.
Just as he had hoped, the movie is just starting and he has the room to himself.  If someone were to show up now, he thinks he'll just "convince" them to move as close to the front and far away from him as possible.  The room is dark and spacious, and Xavier believes he can block out the speakers' sounds if he wants to.  A fine room to contemplate in.
Sitting in the dark room alone he becomes fixated on his mental health.  He tries to latch onto something in his life that will upset him; he is looking for an excuse to cry.  There is a primal instinct in him that if he does so it will be the same as a dog eating grass in order for it to vomit, that he might in the same way clear out his system.  Nothing comes.  He has already dealt with his past and comes to a stark realization: he is happy.  Damn it, how can he be happy when he constantly longs to be a werewolf once again and be among kin, when he feels caught in perpetual isolation and utter loneliness?
Perhaps, old boy, you are perfectly fine.  Pretty sure obsessed people don't know they are obsessed or care to consider it.  Maybe that's it.  If only he had someone to bounce his thoughts off of other than the mirror he used in his mind.  Now this underdog that rises to a shining knight route might not get you the princess, let's be real.  But are you really doing anything wrong?  You heard Gabe, you're helping people.  He wonders if he made any progress in setting himself right, and he thinks he might have taken an imperceptible step forward.  It would have to do.
He watches the movie.
Four
As the screen goes black and white text begins scrolling, he gets up stiffly and walks out.  He wonders if he could make himself levitate around and force his clothes to flutter about as he did so.  From past fictional experiences that always seemed to be a sign that the wizard was exceptionally powerful, and intimidation has its uses.
"Did you enjoy the movie, sir?" Asks the aemon, recovered from his mind warp.  Something in the devil man's voice is reminiscent of "you were alone in there." Perhaps he emphasized the "you" just a tad.
Five or six years ago Xavier thinks a patronizing inflection like that would have made him ball his fists and say something snide.  He can see his boyish self, unmarred by all the heartaches of growing up, turning red and scowling.  The idea is so comical and true that the novian chuckles, which plays eerily into his reply.  The movie was supposed to be a real sympathetic tear-jerker. "It was fine." He said.
It was dusk now, and he was hungry.  He grabbed another healthy burger and soda combo at the pickup window of a Ring Swing and headed toward the edge of town.  He loved how settlements just ended abruptly here on Destursha.  Back on Earth the edge of town was followed by suburbs and rural communities.  In Sul, as in many other Desturshan towns, once Xavier passed up the last boarded up building at the end of the outskirts, there was nothing but rocks and plains, and time to be alone.
He walked into a field deep enough that he could no longer hear the music and scuffles behind him.  He carved a large rock into a crude chair with a few cracking strikes of ice, sat down, and began working on that burger and birch soda.  He needed this time to absorb his situation more fully.  When the food was gone, he incinerated the bagging and cup, and all that was left were his thoughts.
Five
He sat there until the sun passed over the horizon and the moons revealed themselves.  Artemis and Orion were up in the sky, shining their odd colored light on the troubled world below.  The town behind him and the mythical satellites above him had no effect on the sky, and an endless blanket of stars were sprinkled into the void.  There was such a number of them that Xavier wondered how it could still be at all dark there on the surface.  He wondered if the earth was up there somewhere far away.
He wonders also if he and The Order will ever get to breathe the air of their home planet again, and a feeling of homesickness sets into him.  He wonders what he would say to his friends and family if he could see them all again for just a few moments.  Perhaps he would simply say they were in his thoughts, but also he would love to retell his adventures on this alien world.  He wants to see his best friend and tell him that he's missing out.  He wants to see Cathrine again and try to understand why she was so able to tug at his heartstrings and to tell her goodbye.  He wants to be in the comfort of his home and tell his family that he's okay and to please not worry about him.  But he can do none of this.  He cannot call a number to reach home, mail a letter, or shout with all his might.  They're all beyond a wall he cannot surmount.  He hopes they're all holding up well without him.
The air is fanged with frigid teeth, but it doesn't bother him.  Thoughts of home make him feel warm.  There are no clouds, and all that warm air will rise and diffuse and be gone, he thinks.
Behind him the town's lights die and what interference they did produce is now gone.  Only the street lamps still run, and everyone has gone to sleep.  He begins walking back to the Inn and Out.  He gave Gabe and Mara the room key, had said he would get in if he came back before or after them.
The streets are cold and silent, covered in orange hues from the lamps.  Artemis and Orion don't seem to have any effect on the lighting, and to Xavier it all feels artificial.  His solitary footsteps echo in the streets, and that nail of loneliness and homesickness is driven deeper.  The only thing he thinks is missing is a nice breeze to whistle around the eaves of houses and confirm that he is walking through a ghost town.
Six
The motel was in sight, and as he passed an alley between an apartment and a pawn shop, an arm wrapped his elbow and he was pulled almost off his feet into the abysmally dark alley.  There was something cold pressed against his right cheek.
"Get your wallet out!" Demanded a young male's voice, and the cold metal object pressed harder into Xavier cheek.  The novian's arm was still being held, but he supposed he was meant to reach for his wallet with his free hand.  Xavier thought it was quite ironic, because he was carrying a good sum of cash.
"How old are you?" Xavier asked.
The thief jerks his arm. "C'mon man, just get the paper." He's almost whining.  He pushes the metal object against Xavier's face and breaks the skin.  It is a knife.
Xavier heats the handle of the blade until it burns through the young man's glove.  He drops it with a yelp and a "The hell?" Xavier cauterizes his own face and looks up at the young man who is now clutching his right hand with the other and trying to shake off the pain.  He is a silhouette against the dark, black on black.  The man begins running down the alley.
Xavier freezes the man's pants, causing him to fall.  The man throws out a few obscenities and questions, as if this could never have happened to him, the ever clever thief.  The novian approaches the prone man, who is now trying to unbuckle his pants, and lights his way with a hovering flame.  He stands over his attacker, as the man makes a spitting sound, forgetting that he is masked.  Xavier pulls the mask off the man and is surprised there is no attempt to stop him.  He sees a young elf, pale and with a sickly look to his face.  The elf spits at him again.  Xavier hurtles it back, now boiling, at the elf and burns his forehead.  The elf moans.
"Get off, man!  Alright, I ain't gonna steal from ya." He manages to undo his belt and tries to wriggle out of his stone pants.
"Only because I am stronger than you.  What would you have done if I could not defend myself?  Taken my money, sure.  But would you have given me a good poke with that tooth pick also?  I think you might have, and I think you will do it to someone at some point."
"What are you, my mom?  Up yours!  You got no right to tell me how to live."
Xavier sighs.  The elf is making mercy harder and harder.  He unfreezes the pants, and the elf squirms out like a rabid ferret and takes to his feet.  Xavier stops him, not with ice or a wind but just with his mind.  He paralyzes the man upright, the elf's life nothing more than a soft chicken egg in Xavier's hands.  He forces the elf down the alley like a puppet and takes the pants with.  When he finds a tangle of thick pipes jutting from the wall of the pawn shop and into the concrete below, Xavier makes the elf press his back into them.  There is a look of stricken terror on the elf's face as Xavier binds him in place with his pants, fusing the very fabric together so that he cannot untie it.  He releases the elf from his control. "If I should happen to run into you again, and you aren't doing something honest, I'll melt down your knife and make you drink it."
The elf does not reply this time.
Seven
Xavier gets to the door and feels his face.  He doesn't like the line of hardened blood on his cheek.  That isn't something you get just walking through the park or eating a burger.  He guesses this is as good a time as any to start training himself in the art of healing.  He feels the flesh, his own but not truly.  He has to concentrate to feel what is wrong with it, to understand what has been severed and what must be reattached and how.  It isn't so hard, but then again this is a shallow cut and not a torn off appendage.  It's good for practice.  He mends the flesh, no scars, no questions.
The lock on the door works with tumblers.  He feels his way through it almost the same way he did with his face and manipulates the lock just as its key would.  He puts his hand on the doorknob and turns it.  The door opens.
The room is dark, but Xavier can see that both beds are empty.  Standing behind the second bed is a dark figure and a small one.  The taller one is aiming a rifle only Xavier can see, while the shorter is clutching onto a small rectangle as if it were a revolver being readied to draw. "Just me.  I'm fine, and no one followed." Xavier is tired and would like nothing more than to hop into the first bed (though he thinks he might sleep on top of it) and drift away into one of those pleasant dreams.
The first figure lowers its arms and sets the invisible object down against the wall. "You had us worried." Mara says.
Gabe adds, "It's late.  You must have gotten some progress, right?"
Xavier is falling onto the bed.  He wishes it would be as easy as falling into the arms of sleep, to just hit the bed and be out. "Nope." He says and rolls onto his back. "I got a whole lot of nothing."
Mara again. "I don't know what it was like in Bellshire, but everywhere that I've ever seen is dangerous after the lights go off.  It wasn't safe out there on the streets for you, alone and unarmed."
"I am an arm." He says and thinks this might just be the snappiest remark he has ever made.  He thinks the way she phrased that made it seem as if she knew he wasn't really from Bellshire.  Good for her if she's somehow figured me out.  Then she would know that I can handle myself.  "Is there an alarm clock in here?"
"Yes.  Didn't see it earlier." Gabe replies and puts his book away.  The room is still very dark, but none of them bother to flip a switch.
"What time is it now?" Xavier thinks he is using up a substantial amount of energy to spit out that question and stave off sleep for a few more moments.
"Almost one in the morning."
Xavier is glad time works the same here as on Earth.  Less for him to decipher and pretend to feel acclimated to. "Set it for eight, would you?  We all need some rest, but we should get out of here before the sun gets hot."
"How long do you think it'll take to get to Path?"
Xavier liked this abbreviation.  Three syllables was starting to pester him.  He wrests all the remaining thinking power he can muster in this state at rest's doorstep. "If we took a train, we could be there by ten or so.  They'll be checking the trains going into the cities." And I really don't want to put that many people's brains into a spin.  A conductor and an engineer who thought they were moving a train for maintenance was one thing, but if you make fifty people forget the last security check, someone is going to notice. "Walking, which is what we'll be doing, four, maybe five.  It's not all that far."
"I'll set the clock for eight."
Xavier falls asleep on top the motel bed as soon as he hears Gabe finish setting the alarm.  He drifts down, deep into the best dreams of his life.  And when he awakes, he'll remember none of it.

Chapter Fourteen

One
He wakes up twenty minutes before the alarm is set to go off.  He can see their shapes beneath the spread of the second bed.  They are wrapped about each other, and he can't help but give them credit for bravery; the beds could've been cleaner.  He sits up, and there is a smile on his face.  He feels as if he were just doing something pleasant and pushes his mind against the walls of his skull trying to squeeze the memory out, but it won't come.  He looks at the alarm clock, a digital construct that has been bolted to the nightstand between the beds.  It is ten till.
He goes to the bathroom while Mara and Gabe are still asleep and turns on the shower.  He brings in a new pair of his pants and a shirt, good clean stuff, and waits for the water to turn clear and then warm.  He steps in.
He is buckling up his pants when he hears the alarm, and he smiles.  They'll have to wait their turn.
Xavier walks out of the bathroom and past his bed to the door.  Neither Gabe nor Mara comment on him being up early, and he guesses they were expecting it. "I'm going to wait outside.  Get a little bit of air." Mara is walking into the bathroom, so Gabe answers for the both of them with a nod.
Two
The air outside is no longer brisk or refreshing but frosty cold.  Xavier props himself against the wall by their room and breathes in the air readily, as if he might cool down his very core by inhaling enough chilled air.  His thoughts are still whirling with Earth and Salina, but for the first time since getting here to Sul he can feel some focus reserved for the mission.  In the distance he can hear a shrill voice asking for help.  It is raspy and tired sounding, and Xavier recognizes it as his acquaintance from the night before.  He is almost surprised that no one has come to help the lowlife.  If the cavalry wants to wait until after Xavier and his party skip town, he won't spare a moment of worry for it.
Mara steps out and stands against the wall next to him. "So," She begins, "what do you think of The Order?  They had you stationed outside Morphus before anyone else."
Xavier is perfectly fine with the comment and question, but he replies with his reflexes. "How do you know that?"
"Xav, Gabriel and I were some of the first to get there.  And you already had a private camp set up."
"Yeah," He answers and doesn't know why he tried to dodge it. "I thought it would be good to put my talents to constructive use.  I was tired of cleaning up vomit and chasing squatters out of the hospital basement."
"That's all?" She looks down at him, her nonexistent eyebrows furrowed. "The Leviathans would be any adept mage's first choice, if he just wanted to put his skills to good use." She looks out at the empty streets.  The sun has yet to rise over the horizon. "And you're not from Chrissenia, so I'm a bit curious about your motives."
Geez, Hodge was bad enough.  Are you just bad at hiding things?  Since he's beginning to think his tongue betrays him, he only shrugs in response.  It's a weak response, and he knows it, just as he knows he's going to get a follow-up.  You're caving.
"Xav, no one does this kind of work without conviction and motive.  Are you trying to impress someone?"
He feels as though she has dropped a sledgehammer on his head.  He doesn't mind the questioning so much, but she doesn't need to be accurate.  His mind races for a moment.  If this conversation keeps going as it is, he's going to give away more than he can afford. "Seems a little juvenile to be so motivated like that, don't you think?"
"I'd say it's probably one of the strongest motivators in history."
Remember, this is about more than just the one who brought you into this, and who teased you by the campfire, and left you at the mine.  You're doing this to earn your right. "How about this?  I'll share some more after the mission's over.  Extra incentive."
She doesn't reply in any perceptible way.  She readjusts herself against the wall, crosses her arms, and goes back to staring at the street.  Her rifle is pushed to the side so that it isn't scratching against the wall.  The sun has risen.
Three
A few minutes went by of good silence.  Gabe broke this when he came out.  Everyone had their gear and a few supplies.  Xavier went to the check-in, but the door was locked.  There was a mail slot in the door, so he dropped the key into that and found it amusing that it sounded as if it landed on a pile.
The road to Pathosia was lightly worn, grass and weeds with minds to retake the path abounding.  Xavier was just glad that it was a road with plants and not a wrinkled landscape of ankle snapping rocks.
"Hey Mara," Gabe began.  They had been walking for an hour without much talk, and Xavier was happy to hear some form of conversation rise up. "I turned on the news for a minute before I came out of the room.  I guess Andros Steam fell off stage last night."
Andros Steam (real name: Legarius Janus) was the lead singer of Steel Forest and Mara's favorite vocalist. "Did he get hurt?" She asked, genuinely concerned.
"No, I guess some people broke his fall." Gabe was grinning, or at least holding one back.  It seemed to Xavier that Gabe wasn't too broken up about Mara's dream man taking a tumble. "But they did stop the show early, and that caused some fights.  They called in the Leviathans, and guess they showed up right after they were called, probably used one of their aircrafts."
"Glad we're not fighting them." She looked up at the sky as if they might take the compliment. "I don't know how those werewolves ever managed to confront them at all."


Four
They passed up a pair of heavily bundled elves that were huddled together and shuffling their feet toward Sul.  With all the extra bulk they looked like they might be packing oil drums.  Mara and Gabe didn't pay these two any mind, but Xavier was put off by the shivering couple.  Sure, the air had a snap to it, but nothing a light jacket couldn't fix.
Xavier stopped and turned around.  The others did likewise a moment later.  He stared back at the slow moving tanks of cloth and held his hand out from his side, as these, he came to realize, were his revolvers, his six shooters.  Long moments passed, Mara and Gabe came to stand next to him, and the feet shufflers began to slow.
They were in the middle of prairie land when this all happened.  The red sun was behind a wall of silver cloud, but the open golden fields made the day seem as light as ever.  Birds were going south and prairie dogs were chirping like the pests they always seem to be.  Sul was no longer visible, and Pathosia had yet to become.  They were on a fixed plane, a scene unique to itself and sole in the universe.  It would make a fine painting, Xavier thought.
"Highwaymen." Xavier breathed, trying to muffle himself over the echoing expanse.
That's when the great bulk of clothing slid off the two elves like standing socks without a foot.  With one hand Xavier impaled the right with a spire of ice.  With his other he lit the second elf's arms aflame and commanded the fire to engulf the rest of the overly armed man.
Xavier took a second to think and then continued toward Pathosia.  Mara was standing with her rifle halfway drawn, and Gabe just now reaching for his book of incantations.  They shared a glance with one another, a certain understanding passing between the couple.  When both bodies of the elves erupted in pillars of fire, they nodded and followed their leader.
Five
"So Xavier," Gabe began when the bodies were out of sight, "how exactly did you get involved in all this?"
The cold air pushed Xavier's still moist hair against his skull.  Not cold enough to make his hair stiffen, but chill enough to keep the shower water from leaving it. "That's a long story, Gabe.  Not a very interesting one either.  To make the long, boring story short, I was an angsty, confused teenager.  Dime a dozen there."  The wind changed direction and parted his hair, running icy fingers in the rifts against his scalp. "I ran away from home, where everyone had a play-by-play plan for the rest of my life, no say from me.  I picked up a few things about magic on the road, not much if you ask me, but apparently I caught on quick.  I got to the capitol, figured that if I got a job there, the wealth might trickle down to me.  More importantly, I could make my own decisions." Lay it on good and thick.  He doesn't have the strength to read your mind even if he tried. "Out of impulse one day, I decided to sign up for The Order's militia.  Maybe I'd be able to do something more with my skills than mop with no hands and heat up soup.  After some training, here I am." He considered.  It sounded believable to him.  It sounded average. "What about you guys?  You said you were Chrissenians."
There was an exchange between Mara and Gabe, imperceptible at best, paranoia at worst.  Gabe shrugged. "Ours isn't any more interesting." Mara raised her eyes at Gabe when Xavier turned to look at the expanse around them again. "So," Gabe added, "did you have to, ya know, roast those guys back there?"
Probably not.  Xavier answers, "Defend us?  Absolutely.  Those two have killed at least a dozen travelers, and tolled countless others, I'm sure.  Incapacitating them alone wouldn't work."  Let's add a grain of truth to the mix.  He broke away from the subject of the highwaymen, whom he'd killed mostly on impulse. "While I was running away from home, I came to a sort of canyon on the south edge of the Scarab Desert. There were these ogres there, if you could really call them that.  They were impossibly tall, mutants I guess." He can feel the weight of his old sword in his hands, can smell the stench of those behemoth creatures. "They attacked me, probably looking for anything shiny, or maybe they were cannibals.  All I know is that I was definitely not the first to cross their path.  One of them had military tattoos on what you might call his body." He looked for a word, bit his tongue for it, and came up with two. "I think they were the 'Infused' or 'Altered.' That's what Dahzir called his failed experiments.  They're what sometimes live in dark caves, the monsters.  Anyway, I wasn't even half the wizard then that I am now.  But they had me cornered, and I did what I had to." The look of the old general taking that sword and plunging into his own heart. "The one had clearly been suffering, seemed relieved when it was all over."
"That's The Bowl." Mara said.  Xavier's path had been so close to their home. "That's just past where Frander lived."
"I know the forest isn't all that far south of that place, so I'm not surprised you heard of it." Xavier felt warm, as if the sheer thought of that desert was making the world around him hot. "I had to kill those two, and I doubt they were painting the canyon red every day.  It's, as you know, in the middle of absolutely nowhere and not far outside the 'haunted' forest.  But those two elves had a rich road here."
And the subject ended there.
Six
Mara is ahead with her long stride, while the two novians follow behind.  They are still on the road in a vast emptiness that seems to say this whole world is vacant without them.  Far to the west is a range of mountains, and to the east is a great flat that ends in a tinge of green under the horizon.  The smoke from the burning corpses has long since departed and been carried away.  The road stretches on, winding through knolls dotted with wildflowers and oak trees.  It is a comforting place that reminds Xavier of Earth in no specific way but in all ways.  The air here tastes good and feels natural against the lungs.  For a moment he wishes they could just walk this road forever and never reach their destination.
Xavier is walking purposefully, with savoring in each step.  He inhales each breath as if it might be his last, looking for the state of nirvana that seems so close now.  He sees something in the sky over the mountains, something red.  If he were on Earth right now, he could dismiss it, a plane.  He isn't on Earth though, might never be again.  He stops and looks at it, glares at it as if to intimidate the thing which must be miles away.
He tries to get a read on it, but it is simply too far.
Mara and Gabe continue walking, and Xavier forces himself to do the same.
Seven
They stop under one of the oaks as Pathosia comes into view.  It is nestled between green hills and has a river running through the center from west to east.  The buildings are gray with mortar and symmetrically lined with windows.  There were smaller building which were red, and a bland assortment of cream and egg white colored housing structures outlying the city.  A luxury train rides into the city from the northern rails and stops by one of the red structures.  Xavier can see passengers departing and readying to board, and what surprises him most is that there is no visible security checkpoint.
They began walking down that final knoll before the city, as that chill pre-winter wind hastened up the hillside and cooled the pores of their skin and hollows of fur.  Against the wind, as it always had been.  No one complained, and with their target in view, it was hard to notice.  The farther down the hill they went, the stronger the wind seemed to become and the louder the cityscape boomed into life.  With a whistling breeze in his ears, Xavier saw streets packed in with busy morning goers, hustlers and bustlers, and probably more than one shyster.
"Mara," Xavier remembered, "Give me your gun."
She took her rifle off her back and handed it to the novian the way a mother might hand her newborn to an unfamiliar relative.
"Gabe, do I need to take your book?" He continued.
"No." The shorter novian replied. 
"Okay." Xavier had a moment of thought, wishing he'd spent more time thinking before they got to the city. "I'll take the gun and hide it outside the city on the east side.  We split up after this, alright?  But let's meet up every day at dusk where I hide the gun.  I'll do it right along the river." It sounded fine in his head, but coming out it sounded base and unintuitive.
"What do we do if things go south?" Mara asked.  She sounded less confident without her weapon.
Xavier paused.  He didn't want to get any closer to the city and still be discussing this.  The wind bit him in disagreement of his lack of movement. "Gabe, if you can throw up some kind of signal.  Something simple like . . . making a quick couple light flashes in the air."
"I probably could." Gabe replied, but Xavier was unsure of it.
"And Mara just," He had to think, "run east along the river, if you can.  We'll all do that and meet up downstream." Xavier didn't like the odds of fleeing. "Whatever you do, just don't get into trouble.  Please."

Chapter Fifteen

One
Mara and Gabe continued on toward the city streets, while Xavier veered off the road and toward the east of the city.  The rifle in his hands was oversized for him and hefty, not a thing made to be wielded by his kind.  But that weight, cumbersome as it was, gave him comfort.  When magic failed, he supposed you couldn't beat the classic lead and powder.  He slung it over his back, and it drooped low on his small stature.
Off the road was grass taller than he and discarded trash.  A tire from something here that might have been military, a garbage bag there that had been mostly picked clean by scavengers, various sun bleached cans and broken bottles, all of it haphazardly strewn about at random in the tangle of high vegetation.  It didn't look like anyone, not even litterers, had been through here any time even in the last year.
He came to the river past the last of the suburban houses and continued walking.  An urge, reckless and fleeting, passed through him, telling him to just keep going until he reached the ocean.  He considered this passing urge with the same seriousness one might consider streaking through a mall.
He came around an outcropping of rock along the riverbank.  It was part of a boulder on this side of the water, and behind it no one from the city could see.  He toyed with the molecules of the rock and set the rifle against its side.  Then he pushed it into the side, and the rifle began easing into the hard surface as if it was really nothing more than gelatin.  When his arm was elbow deep into the rock-made-pudding, he released his hold on the gun and withdrew his arm.  He returned the rock to its normal state and smiled.  No one would be finding that rifle, not even his companions.
Two
He walked into town from downstream, a bag full of clothes on one side and a pocket full of cash on the other.  It was some time after noon, maybe two or three, but the clouds had grown thick and made it appear to be almost dusk.  So, where to head first?  After careful deliberation, and the aid of a scent that was drifting down the first street, he decided to get some lunch.
The caf he walked into was on the corner of Dante and Halcyon.  He guessed when your city didn't have two thousand streets, you had room to be creative with the names and get outside of the firsts, fourths and sixty-sevenths.  He sat down at a bar and adjusted his bag of clothing behind him like a backpack.  The place was beige and had only the faintest aroma of coffee.  The strongest smells were that of sugars, cinnamon, and vanilla.  There were relaxed customers sitting slouch at booths and in an area that replicated a living room, reading papers and pretending to be able to solve the crossword puzzles.  They all looked to Xavier like what he would call hipsters, just a group of people who thought they were unique by mimicking other people that thought they were unique.
"Can I get you anything?" Asked an elven woman behind the bar.  She was short for an elf, almost dwarfish, and her bleach blonde hair ran down her back all the way to her knees.  She was like a doll.
Xavier stopped surveying the other patrons and took a glance at the menu that hung over a large reflective tank with nozzles and thick paper cups. "I'll take the chicken sandwich and a water." She wrote it down. "You have hot sauce?"
"I'm sorry, sir." She said in the voice of someone readying to be struck. "We only have mayo, ketchup, ranch, mustard, and olive oil."
"That's fine.  The sandwich will be good without it, I'm sure."
"Should we bring you another kind?"
"Ranch will be fine." And he hoped she would just go and put the order in.  His stomach was building up a rage.
"No problem, I got it." She said and handed a slip of paper through a window going into the kitchen.  Then she went on to take the order of a man in a velvet hat.
He looked down at his boots, dirty.  No one else's were, and there was carpeting.  Xavier glanced about and caught a few people gazing at him and whispering to one another.  His first instinct was to think they were trashing him for his drab, filthy attire and his blunt manner of handling his food order.  But no, not these people.  These people would take a look at him and go "There's a cowboy there, or some outlaw.  So totally cool, man." Damn hipsters.
A few minutes went by in which everyone in the place whispered, though he suspected that was normal here.  Only mainstream louts would talk at full indoor voices.  The elf brought him his sandwich, a thing he thought he could eat five of, and a bottle of water that he wondered why he couldn't get immediately in anticipation of his food.  By the time he went to undo the lid of his water, the sandwich had been erased from his plate.  The water went just as fast.
The girl stopped by again with a little slip. "Whenever you're ready, sir."
"I'll take another sandwich to go, if that's alright." If his stomach could have patted him on the back, it would have given him welts.
Three
There was something warming about walking down a cold street with warm food going into the belly.  Probably had something to do with warming blood vessels, he thought and finished off the extra food before the caf was out of throwing distance.
You walked in without so much as a speed bump from the river.  Making a mental note, better not forget.  It was down to business now, business Xavier hadn't the foggiest idea of how to go about performing.
As he drew closer to the center of Pathosia, the air grew warmer and damp.  Steam roiled out of vents along the sidewalks, and scurrying people flitted about to push the warm mist around.  It reminded him of the crowded streets of Fraushein and the endless swarms of people that he never did understand.  By ten in the morning, he was cleaning up vomit in urinals and scraping gum off the sides of X-ray machines, not bustling through the streets.
He hopped onto the sidewalk and did what he could to make himself not appear foreign.  He looked at the street signs but kept moving steadily forward, pretending to know exactly where he was heading.  The crowds closed in and drifted apart like schools of fish.
Someone bumped him hard, and he staggered into a narrow alley between a bicycle shop and a deli.  Xavier fumbled into the wall to keep himself up and wasn't altogether happy with the moist texture of the brick.
"Hey." Came from down the alley.  Xavier was now in full control of his standing and removed his hand from the wall, which took a grit with it, and wiped it off on his pants. "Xavier." The voice said and caught his attention.
Four
The people on the street were as aware of Xavier and the talking alley as they were of Neil Armstrong's visit to the moon, so the novian meandered toward the voice, checking over his shoulder just to be sure.  He passed the bulk of a metal trash tub, a great red thing made by Waste Not Incorporated with maroon colored rust holes eating at the bottom. "Hmm?" He replied as he came around the corner of the bin.
"Ahh sir." An aemon woman with a monotone voice. "I think you dropped your phone, but I found it." Her dark eyes were rotating, checking.  Her horns had been sawed off like a rodeo bull's, and her skin was the same red as the remaining paint on the Waste Not. "I'm sorry I looked through it.  Saw that you only had one contact." Her left hand was holding out a black rectangle with a gray keypad on the front, a throwaway phone.  Her other hand was in the pocket of her tan overcoat, seeming to have a hold of something important.
"Thank you." He took the phone and slid it into a pocket. "I've been a real butterfingers today." She gave Xavier a queer look.  Never heard that one before. "Thanks again."
He walked away, and as he did he turned to look at her.  She was standing in the same spot, smoking a cigarette.  Just someone on break.  He felt the small block in his pocket.  It seemed heavy and deliberate on his thigh.  When he got out onto the street again, he turned it on, no confirmation vibrations or jingles to assure him it was indeed booting up.  The little colorless screen told him hello in a font he thought came straight from a 70s computer, and then it went to a rudimentary menu.  It was three forty seven, and the left side said OWT, which Xavier knew stood for One World Telephonetics.  On either side of the bottom of the screen were the options CONTACTS and MESSAGES, and in between all this was a cloud gray backdrop of nothing.
There was indeed only one contact on the list, but it wasn't a name.  Underneath "Add Contact" is a single entry, even the voicemail and emergency dial numbers seemed to have been wiped clean.  The contact is "Six O'Clock." It's a directive.  He hits END/PWR and is returned to that bare homescreen.  It is ten till four.

Five
An hour passes of him wandering around and getting the gist of the town's layout.  He'll check into a room somewhere and lay down his pack of clothes before he goes snooping.  Too suspicious with a bundle of things swaying on your back, too much like contraband.  
It won't be dusk for another hour.  In another month it'll be dark now, and the month after that night will start shortly after five, but he thinks for now can have a chat with his new friend before his team shows.  He goes into CONTACTS and hits CALL while hovering over the only name to hover over.  It rings once, then twice, a third time.  It stops, and all he can hear is the running water beside him.
"Punctual." Said the earpiece, in a voice he strained to believe. "I like that.  It's orderly.  It's reliable.  And, it means you haven't run into trouble yet."
His hands tingled, and the tips felt just the slightest numb.  But he felt confident. "Hello, ma'am." Could his nervous hands keep the phone from dropping into the stream? "How are you?"
She ignored the question. "Anything to report?"
"No, I just became acquainted with the layout." He waited a moment.  The blood was returning to his digits. "Is there anything I should know?"
"Nothing that you don't already.  Just shut your phone off when you're not calling.  We didn't give you a charge cable, because these things can be hacked at charging docks.  Did you know that?"
He actually did but hadn't thought of it. "No.  But will do."
"Xavier," She sounded familiar, "be careful and take care of Asura and Rosehall.  We'll need the three of you later." The call ended, nice and gentle on the battery.
Six
He held down the END button until the gray screen went black and put the weighty thing back into his pocket.  The sound of the stream came back into reality, and he felt as though everything around him must have paused during that call.  The cold air actually felt cold, and he shivered goose flesh onto his arms.  The sky was beginning to darken, and he saw Gabe and Mara walking from the city along the river.  Time to recap.
He told them where the gun was, but he didn't tell them about the phone.  Mara said the governor didn't have his own building but lived in a penthouse suite at a place called the Spiraling Tower.  Gabe said the Tower was on the north side of the river a few blocks from a military vehicle manufacturing company called Scylla.  He did what he could to fill them in on the place.
"You just can't get into the tower like this." Gabe said and waved a hand over his not outstanding clothes. "The doorman wouldn't let me in the lobby.  I told him I just wanted to check room availability, and he said I could check when I could afford it.  I guess getting bounced like that is part of the Tower's exclusive feel, or whatever."
"Do either of you know if he ever leaves his room?" Xavier asked, a bit jealous of Gabe's fruitful efforts.
Mara replied, "His office is somewhere else, but I don't know where exactly." Her tail swayed into Gabe absentmindedly. "But Festus is unavailable most of the day, and I have a feeling he doesn't just walk out of the Tower and ride a bike to work either."
Xavier nodded. "Anything else?" They looked at each other and shrugged, then shook heads. "I've got nothing either." He looked at them and patted the boulder. "Alright, we'll talk again tomorrow."

Chapter Sixteen

One
The sun had tucked itself under the horizon, and a layer of cloud blocked its corona from creeping over the sky and turning it that golden pink hue.  Night was coming quickly, and with it a chill wind.  Xavier wrapped himself in a shell of warm air as he returned to the city, but he could feel icy daggers slide into his pocket of heat.  He understood that there was a snowstorm coming, the season's first.  If it wasn't that, then it would be an ice storm.
In his experience those were worse.
By the time he found the Paragon hotel, the pack on his back had become heavy and little crystalline flakes had begun floating down from the sky.  The lobby was warm and made him dispel his heat layer before he started sweating.  There was an aemon man at the counter, sitting behind a computer screen that was casting whites and greens and reds onto his dark face.  When he saw Xavier, he leaned forward and tapped the keyboard, and the changing colors turned to a solid and steady white glow.  He clasped his hands together over the pine countertop and waited patiently for the novian to come forward.  The walls around them were painted a forest green, and there were simple wooden supports holding the ceiling up.  No halls leading to an elevator, but there was a hand railed staircase visible through an open door to the right of the clerk.  The man began kneading his fingers, perhaps losing that patience in anticipation of getting back to whatever he had been watching.
Xavier stepped up to the counter and reached into his back pocket for his wallet.  He was alone in the lobby with the clerk, thinking that Desturshans usually settled in for the night before it got dark, a bunch of superstitious jargon for the most part. "I need a room." He said and drew out a handful of cash against the low side of the counter, not wanting to show how much he had just yet.
"When will you be checking out, sir?  We have rooms for the night." The aemon tapped at and clicked at the keyboard and studied the screen with a face that seemed tired of seeing the same information all day. "Some for the weekend, and a few that are unreserved for whole weeks.  What will it be?"
"I'll take one of your long term rooms.  But I'm not sure I'll need weeks."
"That's fine.  We ask for payment for a night one day in advance, and if you choose to leave, simply don't pay and drop off your keys." Another tap. "The ones we have available for the next week are on the second floor, economy rooms.  No maid service, no commodities besides a lavatory, and a twin bed.  Is that alright, sir?"
"That's fine.  I'll only be here to sleep and get clean anyway."
"Alright, may I see a photo ID?"
Xavier handed his over but worked it to make his picture be that of a redheaded dwarven man named Ang Riggs.  By the time the clerk saw the picture, Xavier had his mind convinced that that was precisely who he had been talking to all along.  The clerk handed it back without looking.  He trusted Mr. Riggs.
"Ok. For tonight and tomorrow that'll be seventy." The clerk's eyes were examining the red beard and blocky shoulders of Ang Riggs standing in front of him, but no one was there to tell him that he was staring at a white haired halfling youth.
Two
Xavier paid.  He supposed he could get the room for free, but if the clerk's superiors caught it while Xavier wasn't around to "convince" them otherwise, he might run into snags.  No time for that.  He put his wallet away and readjusted his pack, the core of which he felt had become cold from the outside air.  He put it down on the top of his right foot and let his back have a few moments of respite, while the clerk tapped away at the keyboard and bobbed his head rhythmically.  Xavier realized that it was now he that was becoming impatient.  Standing here, still and warm, made him understand just how exhausted he was.
The aemon gave him a pink piece of paper to sign, which Xavier did as Mr. Ang.  As he handed the binding paper to the clerk, the man exchanged it for a white one, the customer receipt.  A few seconds later the clerk handed the novian a green keycard with a black strip on the rear, #17.
"Your room is out the first door going up the steps, to the right just after rounded the corner of the building." The aemon contorted his arm ridiculously as people do to convey directions other than straight. "If you plan on staying more nights, just say so each evening.  We'll keep it reserved so long as you do.  It'll either be me or Malta." Xavier took this moment to read the man's nametag, which declared him to be Razgul: Paragon Staff.
Xavier took his key and wrapped his bag of clothes around his back again.  As he walked to the stairs, Razgul gave him the imperative to enjoy his stay, to which Xavier hummed a confirmation.
The concrete stairwell echoed with each of his steps, ricocheting back the sound of emptiness.  It made Xavier wonder where Mara and Gabe were staying, and if they were staying together.  Finally some time away from that wizard is probably what they're thinking.  Gabe looked downright hungry when Mara's tail brushed into him earlier.  He was in the hall now, not remembering the steps he took to get here.  His room was before him.  He took that card and slid it through a slat on the door handle.  It unlocked, and he opened it with a sigh of relief.  Good for them.
Three
He flicks on the lights and drops his pack next the bed.  It falls to the ground lightly with a soft whoosh of air.  Something about the bag acting so burdenless makes Xavier scowl at it before taking a trip to the bathroom, where he relieves his suddenly aching kidneys and realizes how hungry he is.  He'll eat tomorrow, after he gets up, after he had the energy to lift a fork to his mouth.  He looks at his face while he washes his hands, and the dark circles under his eyes contrast so strongly with his white hair that he feels like a ragtime robber.
He comes back to the bed, a clean but unadorned thing that he is glad for.  As he stands before it, ready to collapse on it and not worry about the sheets, he considers sleeping the night as his true self.  The idea is enticing, and he feels safe about it.  He'd still have to cover up his scent, sure.  But to be himself again would be a delight.
He runs his mind through the rooms of the Paragon.  Not one person staying or working has the magical potential to shuffle a deck of cards, so he's safe from detection.  He takes a deep breath and wonders if he shouldn't just go to sleep, but he knows this is a skill he should work on while he can.  He starts releasing the hold he has set over his form.  To him it is like shutting off a hose by turning the valve degree by degree.  His clothes get tighter, too tight, far too tight.  He stops and begins working them out, increasing the material proportionally so that it adjusts to him.  He remembers science classes and the laws of conservation, and it baffles him deep inside that this could work, that he could draw upon nothing and change the total amount of energy in the universe.  Like it's magic or something.
His hair changes color to the dull brown of a human's, and there is a growth of coarse fiber on his jawline and under his nose, with thinner outcroppings on his stretching cheeks.  None of that was there the last time he checked.  Bones begin to settle and pop, and enlarged organs work to keep the structure going.  His muscles feel relaxed, as if he'd just released tight bands from around all his arteries.  Oxygen floods into his true form, and he is himself.
He is Cecil again.
Four
He fell down on the bed and kicked his boots off.  Cecil rolled onto his back and stretched.  Oh, it was good to really stretch.  He breathed in, and it was joy to have so much air in such large lungs.  His stomach protested, and even that was good, because it seemed to be justified to be so hungry now.  He ran long fingers through his hair, which felt exactly the same but somehow completely different.  Then he rubbed that steel wool that had grown on his long unattended face.  The beard was short, and covered less of his face than he would like it to.  But that was his face and his hair, not the closest replica he could think of.  No, he was for the first time in what seemed like a whole lifetime himself.
Sleep came easily.
He cursed himself when he awoke that he could be so careless.  He scanned the hotel again, but still the most magical thing aside from him was the recognition system on the doors.  Cecil just hoped no one had come by in the night and sensed what he was, and that would have to be the end of the worrying if he wanted to get anything done.
He walked into the bathroom and turned on the sink.  Despite how Razgul had said there were no commodities, there was a wrapped disposable razor by the sink, some soap, and a can of shaving cream the size of Cecil's real thumb, although it did feel half drained already.  He splashed warm water on his face and coated it in cream.  He had never shaved before, so he didn't know that the glob of gel he squirted into his palm would be enough to shave a mammoth.  He held the razor to his face and then held it down under the warm flowing water for a moment.  Had it been a decade ago when his father went over the basics of shaving with him?  It seemed like it had been some time before he was born, and back then he had nothing to practice on.  He ran it down one cheek carefully, washed it out, and repeated.  It took him twenty minutes to clean up his face, a time he'd like to beat on his next go, whenever that might be.
There.  He thought, butter faced again.  Let's see what it looks like next time.  He shut off the faucet and turned on the shower.
He had forgotten to set the alarm, but he was still up before the sun.  As the hot water ran over the seemingly gargantuan girth that was his human form and he cleaned as routinely as he always had before, he wondered if the Desturshans weren't afraid of the night.  There was almost never a soul on the streets after dark or early in the morning, and he could only think of a time or two when people were rushed to Saint Braun after nightfall, and hadn't they been reluctant to leave until dawn?
Cecil opened up the bag of clothes and pulled a set out.  If he wanted to check out the Tower, he would need better duds.  Or he could persuade the employees into thinking otherwise, but using too much magic that close to an official posed too many risks.  So perhaps the factory would be today's option.  He took a moment to feel like himself again, to relish in truth, before shrinking back down to fit in the clothes he'd bought.
Five
An elven woman, he assumed to be Malta, was sitting at the check-in desk with her legs crossed under a newspaper.  Her eyes were focused on the monitor with her right hand on a steaming coffee mug.  She did not bother herself to look at the little departing guest with his screaming white hair and his man-on-a-mission stride.  All guests thought they were important enough for that, but she disagreed, and Xavier left unnoticed.
Outside was no remnant of that first snowfall on the street, though Xavier could see patches of white on the hills beyond the city lines, wispy sheets that would soon be eaten by the sun.  It was still dark, but only just, and the busy stinking streets were empty for now.  He looked about.  What demon was keeping the people off the streets?  He had seen monsters back in the forest when he returned to life, abominable things that had seemed to have followed him from his nightmares to the real world.  But such things were born of darkness and seclusion (and sometimes labs), and he didn't suppose there would be a nest of those mutants anywhere near Pathosia.
He crossed over the river to the north side and paused a moment to listen to the rushing water.  Despite its glassy texture, the water still sounded alive, not thrashing but alive.  His feet came down on the bridge with solitary importance, and it made him well aware of himself and the acoustics of the buildings surrounding him.  Times like this made him wish he could read the sound waves the way a bat or a dolphin does instead of having to rely upon his magic senses, the ones that could be sensed back.
He hit a pocket of warm air on the other side.  It would seem that this day would be a few degrees warmer than the last, and while that sounded good on a chart, Xavier knew the clouds above would pour ice rain instead of snow.  That was winter's truest danger.  Not that he had to worry about driving in it, but it would at the very least stir up memories of that night he entered Fraushein with that ridiculous sword and all that young courage.  It would remind him of the boy.  Don't call him that.  He wasn't a zit that gets popped and forgotten.  It would remind him of Folas, and Folas would remind him of the mine.  It was all a great turning wheel of bad memories.
People began crawling from the coves which were their homes the moment the light of the cloud impeded sun crested over the long flat expanse of the east.  The filtering light of the sun through cloud gave a cold gray tone to the area reminiscent to Xavier of Halloween.  That set his mind to home and of monsters, ghouls and ghosts, chainsaws and axes, apples and pumpkins, Frankenstein monsters, witches, and, of course, werewolves.  That is what the cold gray represented, and the burning orange of the trees backed the presentation with a gold stamp, absolute confirmation.

Chapter Seventeen

One
Scylla was a long stretch of industrial warehouses, smokestacks, and chain-link fencing.  The front gate was off the street, a guard house accompanying it.  There were patrols moving back and forth outside the buildings.  Men and women, indiscernible under Leviathan armor, strolled along the edges of the buildings and fence, guns in tote.  It was hard to tell racial profiles under armor like that, where the wearers were always covered head to toe in crimson and black plates and walked as uniformly as an assembly robot.  What Xavier was really looking for were mages.  Leviathans of rank had clearance to learn magic, if they showed any aptitude for it, and mages would be able to detect him if he went snooping.  He could try anyway, the more powerful he was, the harder it would be to be detected by a lesser spellcaster, but Leviathans had few trainees out on the line, especially, he supposed, at a place so important.
Xavier needed to know more.  He had a bad feeling that Governor Festus might have a toe dipped into the works here.  Even if he only had a small contingent of Leviathans on his side, taking over the city would be infinitely hardened.  You couldn't impale one of them through their armor, and if you wanted to burn one, you had to be a strong enough caster to see vents and ignore physical barriers.  You could forget about shooting them.  The entirety of their crystal armor was a million times over more bullet proof than anything Earth had ever produced.  So you could send the most skilled wizards, which the Leviathans would also send.  You could send soldiers strong enough to bludgeon the armored troops with such force the trauma did the work, but as far as Xavier knew there had only ever been six people capable of doing that, five now.  He also didn't want to stir up bad relations with the king's old guard, since it was their technology The Order wanted.
Two
One of the patrolmen took notice of Xavier, so the novian began walking, a harmless observation.  Perhaps it was time to check on the Tower.
He made glances at Scylla as he walked down the street, on his way to nothing.  The Leviathans were the sole owners of motorized transport, mostly aerial.  Their land based vehicles could be bought, provided you had troths to burn and the vehicle was decommissioned.  He thought of the van back in Cynderton.  It was clear that passing a driving test was not a requirement in obtaining one of their rides.
After circling the block, Xavier headed toward the plaza where the Tower was.  He reasoned that there was a very real possibility that out of convenience there might be a clothing store of some sort with attire "suitable" to be worn in the presence of the rich.  It was a ridiculous notion to think expensive clothes were a form of visa, but he knew loathingly that it was true.  Then he had to consider just what it was he was going to do once he got inside.  A stupid man would come right out and say he had an engagement with the governor, but what exactly would a brilliant man say?  
He would have to come up with that.
Three
The district with the Tower starts at Ouro Square, and ends at the city line.  One could see a literal division, seeing the square and what kind of bricks they used to pave.  Any other place in Pathosia had slate red bricks that may or may not all be in the best condition.  Here the bricks are painted a velvet blue and shine with a polished glare.  The buildings look cleaner, and the people walk straighter and taller.
In front of him is the square, and beyond that are two perpendicular streets, one heading west and the other north.  It is quieter here than it was on the south side, almost solemn.  In the center of the square is a black marble fountain with sculptures of what Xavier believes are seraphim, not cherubim, encircling the spout, which is shooting a stream straight up.  The street going east is lined with presentable green lawns and rigid iron fences.  In one of the nearer yards is a group of stunted trolls toiling over a patch of flowers, while a wolf dogman observes them from behind a window.  The northern street is crowded with bakeries and jewelry shops, and a pleasant aroma drifts from that direction.  Xavier also notices a lack of steam vents leaking less than desirable mist onto the streets here.  He can feel the landscape give off an uppitiness that makes his stomach knot in disgust, and he heads north.
The sickness in his stomach turns to hunger the moment he passes the first bakery.  There are tarts and cakes in the window, but he isn't convinced that they are anything more than displays.  Even without walking up to the broad see-through glass, Xavier spies a tray of Danishes behind a sneeze guard, and that sends his gut into a tumble of angry and futile noises.  There are people inside eating at tables and sipping something hot from small white cups.  They are all acting dignified, as if they eat only because they must.  The jewelry stores are closed, and he doesn't think they'll make him any hungrier besides.  Then he comes upon other restaurants, and his insides turn hostile.  Luckily every place he passes is signed with a "Dress Attire Only." Seeing that time and time over brings his stomach back to disgust and curbs whatever appetite the smells had built up.
Four
The north street intersects with another that has a travel agency, a servant hiring service, and an office building that claimed to be a law firm.  Across from this street is one with three small but very fine residential houses and two that were up for sale.  He continues northward and ignores these offshoots.  Ahead maybe seven or eight blocks is a tall glass plated structure that his mind reasons should be the tower.
He is aware that people are staring at him and his dirty boots and plain clothes.  Even without magic, Xavier can feel their eyes boring into him, can almost hear the murmurs they make to one another.  Such things as "I think he must be lost." And "I hope none of us ever end up like one of them." It's not that he minds these highfalutin people and their twisted view of reality, but he does wonder if he shouldn't be more covert.  Rich people had a way of thinking the lower classes were composed primarily of scum.  His cover could be blown by one of the snobs looking to purge dregs from this noble society.  Xavier could hear it now, a woman clad in garments more expensive than three months of his rent in Fraushein speaking to one of Festus's police. "Yes," She would say, and in a way that made it seem painful for her to even talk of such things, "I saw a man, a novian that is, white hair and dirty clothes.  Oh, he did not look like he belonged here.  I don't mean that racially, heavens no.  Only that's what he was, and his shirt, the bawdiness.  I could practically smell him all the way from inside my house." That wasn't even a tenth enough to convict Xavier of anything, but it would be enough to make people aware.
With the Tower still three blocks from him, Xavier found a men's clothing store.  He was beyond certain that it would not be like the one he visited just days before.  This store was called Helios Fine Wares, the kind of place that made you want to buy upscale clothes just to come in and buy theirs.  There were men in suits being measured by on-hand tailors and assistants walking about with hands clasped neatly behind their backs, ever in search of a customer to help.  There were walls of various suit sizes, broken up in category by size and race.  Two aisles of shoes, polished to shine like the store's namesake, ran forward from the rear.  The lighting was soft and inaudible, no florescent and no ordinary watt either, as all the lights appeared to be hand made to look like the red sun.  It was all impeccably clean and sterile and caused Xavier to reconsider his Tower strategy.
Five
That's when an elven man resembling Partheus approached him. "Can I help you, sir?" His ability to hide his disdain was incredible.  He wore what the novian had always thought of as a "penguin" suit, which came with a bowtie.  The elf was thin, but the shoulders of his garb gave the illusion of broadness.
Xavier looked at the elf, and then at the store, and then at himself.  A frown was dragging his face into the floor, and there wasn't a thing he could do to stop it.
